  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_90964fcf-8cd7-41f9-80de-21a04cf5517d'
      });

  <span id="freeText9198135352605525538" style="display:none">"Penman's characters are so shrewdly imagined, so full of resonant human feeling that they seem to be on the page....Most compelling is the portrait of the Welsh as wild and rugged as their landscape."<br />SAN FRANCISCO CHRONICLE<br />Here, alive from the pages of history, is the compelling tale of a Celtic society ruled by Llewelyn, Prince of Wales, on a collison course with a feudal realm of Edward I. WIth this last book in the extraordinary trilogy that began with HERE BE DRAGONS and continued in FALLS THE SHADOW, Sharon Kay Penman has written a beautiful and moving conclusion to her medieval saga. For everyone who has read the earlier books in this incomparable series or ever wanted to experience the rich tapestry of British history and lore, this bold and romantic adventure must be read.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

            swapContent(lessLink);
          }

<div id="review_42091373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42091373" />
    <a title="April" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1392934-april"><img alt="April" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551286895p2/1392934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42091373?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April" href="/user/show/1392934-april">April</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42091373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14418840436079536599">My gosh. All I can say is I'm so sad it's over. This was by far the best trilogy I have ever read. Some day I will go back and read them all over again.<br/>Penman can introduce a ton of characters and somehow she writes where you can keep them all straight in your head. She makes you FEEL for these characters until you think you actually know them. I caught myself slowing down and wanting to stop reading because I didn't want it to end! Wonderful. Everyone should read this trilogy! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_247620870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247620870" />
    <a title="Rio (Lynne)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803025-rio-lynne"><img alt="Rio (Lynne)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441050255p2/3803025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247620870?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rio (Lynne)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rio (Lynne)" href="/user/show/3803025-rio-lynne">Rio (Lynne)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312382476" href="/book/show/6081190-the-reckoning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803025-rio-lynne?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247620870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10464004371845572951">This was the third book in this engrossing and fulfilling trilogy. In book 1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77449.Here_be_Dragons__Welsh_Princes___1_' title='Here be Dragons (Welsh Princes, #1) by Sharon Kay Penman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here be Dragons</a> we are introduced to Llywelyn the Great. He was The Prince of Wales for over 40 years. In Book 2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_' title='Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falls the Shadow</a> we see the rising of Simon de Montfort who fought for the people of England's civil rights and the continuation of the English and Welsh wars. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_' title='Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falls the Shadow</a> continues the family drama of Llywelyn's children and his grandchild and namesake Llywelyn aka Llelo. In this final trilogy, without </span>
  <span id="freeText10464004371845572951" style="display:none">This was the third book in this engrossing and fulfilling trilogy. In book 1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77449.Here_be_Dragons__Welsh_Princes___1_" title="Here be Dragons (Welsh Princes, #1) by Sharon Kay Penman" rel="nofollow noopener">Here be Dragons</a> we are introduced to Llywelyn the Great. He was The Prince of Wales for over 40 years. In Book 2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_" title="Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman" rel="nofollow noopener">Falls the Shadow</a> we see the rising of Simon de Montfort who fought for the people of England's civil rights and the continuation of the English and Welsh wars. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_" title="Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman" rel="nofollow noopener">Falls the Shadow</a> continues the family drama of Llywelyn's children and his grandchild and namesake Llywelyn aka Llelo. In this final trilogy, without giving too much away a grown up Llelo aka Llywelyn The Last continues to fight the English for an independent Wales. King Edward, like King John just refuses. <br /><br />I went into all three books not knowing about the Welsh wars and knowing little about Simon de Montfort. As I was told, do not google as you read, for the stories are all page turners and you want to be surprised. Penman as usual sticks to a lot of historical accuracy, which is why you don't want to google until the end. So many of these scenes were just incredible, but true! Some characters as she mentions were real, but little was known about them. Overall, most people when they think of English wars with the surrounding countries think of the Scottish wars. The Welsh ones were just as interesting. Read these in order to get the complete experience. Fascinating reads! Deep character involvement and how can you not get attached when you start with the Grandparents in Book 1 and get to know these characters from their births and experience their whole lives? A 5 Star Trilogy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10464004371845572951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6588799535791995840" style="display:none">The Greatest Trilogy of all time! <br /><br />In my entire history of reading, no book(s) have affected me the way SKP’s Welsh Trilogy has. This entire trilogy was so engrossing, beautiful, heart rending and a fantastic adventure. I fell totally and completely in love with Wales and her people. SKP’s books are so historically accurate with just enough added drama, you just can’t help fall in love with these characters. <br /><br />This particular book “The Reckoning”, which concludes the trilogy, has been on my night stand for a few weeks with the last 100 pages of the book still to be read. When I finished I wanted no interruptions (my life recently has become out of control busy) for I knew I would be completely heartbroken for it to end. <br /><br />I feel my words just don’t convey the greatness of these books but, I highly recommend this trilogy to all!! “Here Be Dragons” the first is my favorite! And what’s not to love about that awesome title! I just discovered SKP this year and she has rapidly topped my list of favorite authors. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2112894063826680736">So far, this has been one of the best book series I’ve read, and undeniably one of the most heart-wrenching, too. I think the last time I have allowed myself to become this dreadfully upset over a book and ended up being a monumental cry-baby was after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77203.The_Kite_Runner' title='The Kite Runner by Khaled Hosseini' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Kite Runner</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/753065.A_Dog_of_Flanders' title='A Dog of Flanders by Ouida' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Dog of Flanders</a>.   <span id="freeText2112894063826680736" style="display:none">So far, this has been one of the best book series I’ve read, and undeniably one of the most heart-wrenching, too. I think the last time I have allowed myself to become this dreadfully upset over a book and ended up being a monumental cry-baby was after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77203.The_Kite_Runner" title="The Kite Runner by Khaled Hosseini" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kite Runner</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/753065.A_Dog_of_Flanders" title="A Dog of Flanders by Ouida" rel="nofollow noopener">A Dog of Flanders</a>. I never realized I’d actually foster the same sentiment for Simon de Montfort and the two Llewelyns who lived so many centuries ago, came from halfway across the globe, and did not even grace the pages of our World History textbooks. This series has led me to appreciate and respect these heroes and the causes they fought for, to shed a considerable volume of tears I never thought I actually possessed (as I don’t cry that easily), and for that alone, Miss Penman deserves more than 5 stars from me. <br /><br />Anyway, I was supposed to write an objective review about this book, but my mind is still in 13th century Wales and brooding over the many “what ifs”—however foolish—that this book/series has conjured up. <br /></span>

<div id="review_159103347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159103347" />
    <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship"><img alt="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325201543p2/5229326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159103347?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship">Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=wales">wales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159103347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4686752141777767726">The Reckoning is a solid read and a better book than Falls the Shadow, so I give it four stars despite some reservations. <br/><br/>This last installment of Penman's Welsh trilogy covers the years 1271-1283, as Edward I wages war on Wales in his determination to bring the entire island under English rule. Llewelyn ap Gruffyth, grandson of Llewelyn Fawr, is Prince of Wales and, in the same vein as his grandfather, is determined that Wales remain independent and united. Other Welsh lords, most notably Llewe</span>
  <span id="freeText4686752141777767726" style="display:none">The Reckoning is a solid read and a better book than Falls the Shadow, so I give it four stars despite some reservations. <br /><br />This last installment of Penman's Welsh trilogy covers the years 1271-1283, as Edward I wages war on Wales in his determination to bring the entire island under English rule. Llewelyn ap Gruffyth, grandson of Llewelyn Fawr, is Prince of Wales and, in the same vein as his grandfather, is determined that Wales remain independent and united. Other Welsh lords, most notably Llewelyn's brother Davydd, resent his leadership and make unreliable allies at best. This sets the stage for a series of high-stakes wars. <br /><br />As always with Penman, I learned a fair bit of history from this book. Additionally, it is much better-plotted and more cohesive than Falls the Shadow. It helps that this one only spans 13 years, making it much easier for the reader to stay in touch with the characters' lives. As the book rushes toward its dramatic conclusion, the plot is focused and well-paced. It also helps that these characters had eventful lives; there's even a pirate attack, which is very well-done. <br /><br />But while Penman is a much better character writer than your average historical novelist, this book is not the best example of her talents (or I've simply read too many of them). Llewelyn is a Standard Penman Hero and almost indistinguishable from his grandfather: he's totally devoted to his cause, he's brave, he's a loving husband; if he has a flaw it's that he's a bit self-righteous. Ellen has her moments (as do the other de Montforts, for certes), but she's quite similar to previous heroines, and while the build-up to her eventual meeting with Llewelyn is excellent, their actual relationship seems like a mishmash of relationships in previous Penman books. <br /><br />Meanwhile, several supporting characters, while sympathetic and with interesting stories to tell, are primarily characterized by their loyalty to the principals, making them very similar to each other and to other Penman supporting characters. And Edward I makes a good villain, but he's not the complex character study that Kings John and Henry III were; he's mostly just a villain, brave but power-hungry, determined to believe himself a good guy even if it requires self-delusion. Edmund, his supportive younger brother, seemed a carbon copy of Richard, King John's supportive illegitimate son. None of these characters are flat by any means, but they're not quite as complex as previous protagonists, and share too many traits with those same previous protagonists to be particularly memorable. Davydd stands out as perhaps the most complex of the bunch, and his troubled relationship with Llewelyn is an apt focal point for this story. <br /><br />The writing itself is good, aside from Penman's excessive fondness for the comma splice. And while her dialogue--always competent--improved as of Falls the Shadow when she stopped overusing auxiliary verbs in an effort to make it sound more archaic, I do find the sheer amount of banter included in this book odd, given that none of it is remotely humorous on the page. To be fair, the jokes are apparently intended to illuminate the characters' relationships and show that they have a sense of humor even under pressure, not to make readers chuckle; still, it's a bit overdone. <br /><br />Finally, while we do see something of the characters' everyday lives, I feel a bit shortchanged when it comes to immersion in the culture in which the characters lived. This may be unfair to Penman--particularly as I just finished reading Anya Seton's Katherine, where the author takes a far more anthropological interest in 14th century England--but while this book is without a doubt solid on its historical information and psychological truths, its picture of 13th century life is sketchy. England doesn't feel different from Wales or France, aside from a few references to the terrain; Penman's 13th century is much like her rendering of the 12th or the 15th. Italy has its own character, but the rest of the world depicted here has the same generic backdrop of castles and abbeys, servants and prostitutes. Maybe the life of the nobility really was the same everywhere; still, to me at least, the scene-setting felt rather perfunctory. <br /><br />I recommend this book to those who enjoyed the first two; it could also be read independently, as Penman does a good job of getting the readers up to speed at the beginning, but one who started here would miss the background and the protagonists' young lives. The book does a solid job of finishing the trilogy; the end is sad, but well-done. An enjoyable reading experience, if not without flaws. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4686752141777767726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_236505737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236505737" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579036502p2/6773727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236505737?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=need-reviewing">need-reviewing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=books-reviewed">books-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236505737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12646789518406924859"><u>This book concludes the trilogy to a wonderful Historical novel, centering around the vying powers of Wales and England.</u> It is written in a manner where most readers can relate to the powers on both sides . .. difficult to do especially in the second and third book, when Longshanks or Edward I, comes into the spotlight.<br/>Wales is losing ground and, for the first time, England has a powerful ruler who can take advantage of it. And, he does.<br/><br/>And, as the rulers of Wales plot against each other, Edward</span>
  <span id="freeText12646789518406924859" style="display:none"><u>This book concludes the trilogy to a wonderful Historical novel, centering around the vying powers of Wales and England.</u> It is written in a manner where most readers can relate to the powers on both sides . .. difficult to do especially in the second and third book, when Longshanks or Edward I, comes into the spotlight.<br />Wales is losing ground and, for the first time, England has a powerful ruler who can take advantage of it. And, he does.<br /><br />And, as the rulers of Wales plot against each other, Edward grows stronger. He even marries off one of his cousins, hoping to make the strongest Welsh prince, come to his way of thinking but it does little good.<br /><br />This is where the third book starts . . . and where it ends. Fans of the Welsh side should be warned that this tale will be bittersweet to tragic.<br /><br />Tale is lyrical and unlike the previous novel tends to slow down in pace in certain chapters hence the four stars over the usual five in the series. Still very good, though.<br /><br /><b>REVISION NOTE AS OF 09/05/03:</b> I have re-read THE RECKONING so my memory if far more clear. The beginning of this novel is truly a conclusion to the Montfort Family from the second book. As some will recall, this is the family that lost to the English King and had to retreat to France. It is there that old wounds are gradually healed, the Montforts continue upward, or downard, in their lives and the family is connected back to England through a broken plight troth: prince Lwellyn of Wales to Eleanor de Montfort.<br /><br />But unlike his grandfather, Lwellyn Fawhr, Lwellyn ap Gruffyd has more brothers, who are out to fight and betray him; a stronger English King who has the drive and strategy to absorb Wales into the Kingdom, and a number of incidents, resulting in bad fortune. In addition, Lwellyn's bride is captured by Edward I and held for three years before she is finally freed. By the time she is freed, Edward has forced Lwellyn to give up territories and privileges.<br /><br />So, by the time Lwellyn goes to war against Edward, a portion of Wales has already been partitioned off. In addition, a fatal wound and no heir, leaves Wales in turmoil, leaving Edward I the advantage of taking over the country.<br /><br />Note that Edward I was also Longshanks, who was the English King in BRAVEHEART. A fine movie but not entirely accurate in the Historical sense, since the French princess was 7, Edward I had many more children, there was no bridge shown at the Battle of Stirling and people tended to wear helmets to protect themselves in such bloody fights. Lastly and obviously, there was no bastard son born from Wallace and the princess. Nice dramatic punch though.<br /><br /><b>STORY/PLOTTING: B to B plus; CHARACTERS/DIALOGUE: B plus to A minus; HISTORICAL FLAVOR: B plus to A minus; HISTORICAL ACCURACY: B plus to A minus; LOVE STORIES: B minus to B; WHEN READ: January 2013 (3 reads); OVERALL GRADE: B to B plus. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12646789518406924859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1262769507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1262769507" />
    <a title="Deborah Pickstone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37849334-deborah-pickstone"><img alt="Deborah Pickstone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432503842p2/37849334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1262769507?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Pickstone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Pickstone" href="/user/show/37849334-deborah-pickstone">Deborah Pickstone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312382476" href="/book/show/6081190-the-reckoning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=favourite-authors">favourite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=human-nature">human-nature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=uk-fiction">uk-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=lets-be-pacifists">lets-be-pacifists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=my-historical-heroes">my-historical-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=moral-dilemma">moral-dilemma</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37849334-deborah-pickstone?shelf=myth-and-legend">myth-and-legend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1262769507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16670769976922426926">Edward I, Edward Longshanks, Hammer of the Scots doesn't even get a mention in a list of Worst Kings of England. The usual suspects appear (along with a couple of Queens, which scarcely seems fair). For me, there is no question - he was the worst, the very worst King England ever had. We use the word 'ruthless' these days as if it were a concept in and of itself - ruth has become an archaic concept; it means 'a feeling of pity, distress or grief'. Compassion. Edward had little of any of that - h</span>
  <span id="freeText16670769976922426926" style="display:none">Edward I, Edward Longshanks, Hammer of the Scots doesn't even get a mention in a list of Worst Kings of England. The usual suspects appear (along with a couple of Queens, which scarcely seems fair). For me, there is no question - he was the worst, the very worst King England ever had. We use the word 'ruthless' these days as if it were a concept in and of itself - ruth has become an archaic concept; it means 'a feeling of pity, distress or grief'. Compassion. Edward had little of any of that - he was ruthless.<br /><br />He also had a firm belief that God wanted him to.....do exactly as he pleased, which meant hammering Scots, going on Crusade to hammer infidels, decimating the Jewish population of England and annihilation of the Welsh, who it pleased him to see as being in rebellion against him. Except that they weren't part of England so it's a bit of a trick for me to see how they were rebels. Howsomever.<br /><br />The story of the death fight of the Welsh, the fratricidal fractures that helped and the story of Llewelyn ap Gruffydd and Ellen de Montfort is told with pretty faithful adherence to the history as it is known and is certainly brought to life. It is only bettered by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/409419.The_Brothers_of_Gwynedd__Brothers_of_Gwynedd__1_4_" title="The Brothers of Gwynedd (Brothers of Gwynedd #1-4) by Edith Pargeter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Brothers of Gwynedd</a>. Ms Penman is into her stride in her writing by the time she wrote this final novel dealing with Welsh history and it is a riveting read.<br /><br />Sadly, history seems to value the 'Warrior King' (Edward) rather than vilify him as a cheating, lying, vindictive, vicious, arrogant bully. He won, natch. He was followed by Edward II who <i>does</i> make it onto the list, having been a 'weak' king who preferred chaps and gave lots of money to his 'favourites'. He wasn't, though, responsible for the huge loss of life and general public mayhem that was his father's legacy to his own country. If I could travel back in time and change on thing in history - Sultan Baibers' assassin would have been successful in 1272.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16670769976922426926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11652990204133062912"><b>Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>The final book in Penman's <i>Welsh Princes</i> series is even better than the first two; less political, more emotional, and in the last 100 pages, totally heartbreaking. <br/><br/>Adorable little Llelo from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_' title='Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falls the Shadow</a> has grown up into Llewelyn, Prince of Wales, as courageous as his namesake grandfather from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77449.Here_be_Dragons__Welsh_Princes___1_' title='Here be Dragons (Welsh Princes, #1) by Sharon Kay Penman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here be Dragons</a>, and facing the same adversaries in the form of treacherous kin and arrogant kings. And talking of kings, I hated Edward I in this, <i>hated</i> him. What a dirty, double-de</span>
  <span id="freeText11652990204133062912" style="display:none"><b>Rating: 4.5 stars</b><br /><br />The final book in Penman's <i>Welsh Princes</i> series is even better than the first two; less political, more emotional, and in the last 100 pages, totally heartbreaking. <br /><br />Adorable little Llelo from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_" title="Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman" rel="nofollow noopener">Falls the Shadow</a> has grown up into Llewelyn, Prince of Wales, as courageous as his namesake grandfather from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77449.Here_be_Dragons__Welsh_Princes___1_" title="Here be Dragons (Welsh Princes, #1) by Sharon Kay Penman" rel="nofollow noopener">Here be Dragons</a>, and facing the same adversaries in the form of treacherous kin and arrogant kings. And talking of kings, I hated Edward I in this, <i>hated</i> him. What a dirty, double-dealing, unrelenting git.<br /> <br />The book had me in tears twice <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[for the tragic deaths of first Ellen and then Llelo <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Both those chapters were unbearably and beautifully moving, a desperate end to a doomed story. But still there’s more, with Edward’s final acts of spiteful vengeance. I sat in silence for a while after finishing, taking in the full story from all three books, all filled with so much hope and so much sadness.<br /> <br />The <i>Welsh Princes</i> trilogy is one of the best series' I’ve read.<br /> <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3363474875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14273668138775133616"><i>Wales will endure. Scriptures tell us so, tell us that one generation passeth away, and another generation cometh, but the earth abideth forever. We must remember that in the dark days that lie ahead.</i><br/><br/>Was it a good ending of the series? Can I call it so thinking of what befell with Wales?<br/><br/>What to add? <b>A magnificent saga. Great stories, great (but not flawless) people. The touching events. Phenomenal historical accuracy (even about quite bizarre happenings).</b><br/><br/>I would have liked to read such novels ab</span>
  <span id="freeText14273668138775133616" style="display:none"><i>Wales will endure. Scriptures tell us so, tell us that one generation passeth away, and another generation cometh, but the earth abideth forever. We must remember that in the dark days that lie ahead.</i><br /><br />Was it a good ending of the series? Can I call it so thinking of what befell with Wales?<br /><br />What to add? <b>A magnificent saga. Great stories, great (but not flawless) people. The touching events. Phenomenal historical accuracy (even about quite bizarre happenings).</b><br /><br />I would have liked to read such novels about the whole history - it would be pure pleasure and a memorable lecture.<br /><br />I should write a very long review, considering how excellent the book (and the saga) was but I am too full of these superb stories to have a place for my own words.<br /><br />PS I have had a very realistic dream tonight. I was a 'cariad' for someone who was a mix of two Llewelyns and Simon. I was pregnant and he had to go for war (for Wales, of course). And he didn't come back. When I heard he died my heart broke. The feeling of sorrow, of despair, was so deep and real that after waking up I had to think for a while to myself that it was just a dream. I don't recall now which other <b>book touched me so deeply to be able to create such a dream</b> (although I am sure there were a few).</span>

<div id="review_454855944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454855944" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2842201-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420648343p2/2842201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/454855944?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/2842201-robin">Robin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10885948-the-reckoning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2842201-robin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2842201-robin?shelf=13th-century">13th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2842201-robin?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2842201-robin?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2842201-robin?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2842201-robin?shelf=wales">wales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer454855944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15842821422505624065">This one was definitely the most emotional book out of the trilogy - actually, it’s the most emotional SKP book I’ve read yet. Though I always enjoy Penman’s characterizations, I got so attached to the characters in this one <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[that I was really depressed when certain inevitabilities happened. I think that’s why Penman introduced Hugh and Caitlin - they served as fictional protagonists that she could actually give a happy ending to. But even that was kind of bittersweet, knowing all </span></span>
  <span id="freeText15842821422505624065" style="display:none">This one was definitely the most emotional book out of the trilogy - actually, it’s the most emotional SKP book I’ve read yet. Though I always enjoy Penman’s characterizations, I got so attached to the characters in this one <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that I was really depressed when certain inevitabilities happened. I think that’s why Penman introduced Hugh and Caitlin - they served as fictional protagonists that she could actually give a happy ending to. But even that was kind of bittersweet, knowing all they’d lost too.<br /><br />You know an author is great at what they do when they can take a character who tried to assassinate the main protagonist, his own brother, and convince the reader to empathize with him by the end. I was so devastated for Davydd and his family at the end - but then, he did do a lot of growing up in the second half of the book.<br /><br />I was also devastated for Wales and the Welsh, though I’ve only ever been there once and have no prior attachments or associations with them, SKP makes you feel for them wholeheartedly nonetheless. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I know that Edward I was known for his ruthlessness and this novel really does an excellent job at portraying why.<br /><br />At the risk of sounding like a fangirl, this is the best book I’ve read in the last couple years. I do think it’s worth reading the first two books in the series too, since they are also excellent books and it’s worth reading all the build up to the climax in this one. But this one really moved me in a way the others didn’t, in a way that a book hasn’t for a while.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15842821422505624065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8760829176114105640" style="display:none">What a great book. Along with an engrossing story I learned much about English history that I had never heard of before. I have to admit, some of the things that came up during the courtship/marriage of Llewellen and Ellen seemed absolutely bizarre, and then I searched the internet on these characters and they did actually happen. Edward I was and is an absolute two timing double faced snake in the grass!! <br /><br />I won't give it away, but a scene at the end of the book was so heartbreaking I literally cried for about 10-15 minutes. I can't recall any other book affecting me so. This was an awesome series, Here Be Dragons, Falls the Shadow and the Reckoning. </span>

<div id="review_488382163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488382163" />
    <a title="Karen Brooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2382210-karen-brooks"><img alt="Karen Brooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450143415p2/2382210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488382163?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Brooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Brooks" href="/user/show/2382210-karen-brooks">Karen Brooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488382163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12798202702051144527">Sometimes, it’s really difficult reading the novels of a writer whom you know takes great pains to be historically accurate while still telling a sweeping, dramatic and emotionally fraught tale. So it is with Penman who, in this last book of The Welsh Prince series, brings the story of the struggles of the Welsh prince, Llewelwyn, and the machinations of Edward Longshanks, King of England, to a close. <br/>For those who know the history, you understand the ending is not a happy one and it’s this that</span>
  <span id="freeText12798202702051144527" style="display:none">Sometimes, it’s really difficult reading the novels of a writer whom you know takes great pains to be historically accurate while still telling a sweeping, dramatic and emotionally fraught tale. So it is with Penman who, in this last book of The Welsh Prince series, brings the story of the struggles of the Welsh prince, Llewelwyn, and the machinations of Edward Longshanks, King of England, to a close. <br />For those who know the history, you understand the ending is not a happy one and it’s this that makes the novel difficult reading. The tale of Llewelyn’s reign, his marriage, love, triumphs and losses, his turgid and troubled relationship with is brother, the complex Davyd, are all explored in wonderful, deep and moving ways. Likewise, Edward’s motivations, the relationship he has with not only his brother and cousins, but also his conscience, which appears to conveniently massage events and consequences to suit his purpose, are all told with such emotional truth, you both delight and ache for the characters and the futures that await them. <br />I adored this book – as I have all the others in this series and, indeed, by Penman. She is a historical novelist par excellence – in that she manages to balance both the history and the story-telling so very well. Lost in the chaos and turmoil of the era, the bloodshed, treachery and religiosity, the story is also laced with romance, honour, adventure (including pirates!) and betrayal. <br />As is usual with Penman’s work, she brings the female characters (those often diminished or elided by history) particularly to life, representing them as strong, brave, fully-rounded women who while they may not be on the frontline in the physical sense as battles and politics rage around them, nonetheless form the backbone and emotional rearguard upon which their men (husbands, brothers, fathers, cousins and sons) will rely to succour them.<br />From Ellen to Eleanor to Nell, they are three-dimensional, amazing women who loved their men – faults and all – and in the end, it’s they who bear the heavy cost of their loyalty and love.<br />A superb conclusion to a tumultuous and possibly lesser known period of history, I cannot recommend this series (or any of Penman’s novels) highly enough. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12798202702051144527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1655250957" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655250957" />
    <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites"><img alt="Lisa (Harmonybites)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337396485p2/2596042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655250957?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa (Harmonybites)" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites">Lisa (Harmonybites)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655250957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2814300421899202919">I can now say I've read all of Penman's novels, a baker's dozen of them, and my favorites remain The Sunne in Splendour and the first novel in the Welsh Princes trilogy, Here Be Dragons. I'd say this ranks just the next level down--a four and a half, rather than a five. Not to be counted among my favorite books of all time and it didn't move me to tears--but great as historical fiction nevertheless. I'm newly impressed with Penman's skills as a historical novelist. Her research is evident, she d</span>
  <span id="freeText2814300421899202919" style="display:none">I can now say I've read all of Penman's novels, a baker's dozen of them, and my favorites remain The Sunne in Splendour and the first novel in the Welsh Princes trilogy, Here Be Dragons. I'd say this ranks just the next level down--a four and a half, rather than a five. Not to be counted among my favorite books of all time and it didn't move me to tears--but great as historical fiction nevertheless. I'm newly impressed with Penman's skills as a historical novelist. Her research is evident, she definitely conveys how alien the medieval mindset was compared to our times but makes her characters relatable. It can't be easy, fleshing out these stick figures we get mere outlines of from chroniclers, putting actions and words that fit.<br /><br />If anything, that was the problem as I reached the end of the book. I dreaded that ending and it made me drag my feet those last hundred pages. In fact, I had deliberately avoided the last two books in this trilogy for years. Here Be Dragons is a true life love story--among the most moving I'd ever read, all the more for being based on real people. As a love story, it's has it's share of the bitter among the sweet, but of all of Penman's books I'd say its the most upbeat. But the other two? Well, anyone who knows anything about British history would know that it wasn't long after the events of that book that Wales was swallowed into England. The very titles of the books gave me pause: "Falls the Shadow" and "The Reckoning." If that weren't enough, well, Penman is all to good at showing the flaws and foibles of the characters that doomed them--and poor Wales. All at the same time making medieval Wales terribly appealing to a modern reader. At the same time she doesn't demonize Edward I--but you want to damn him thoroughly anyway!<br /><br />And now, if you'll excuse me I think I'll begin the process of Penman withdrawal by finding the fluffiest, more sickening sweet and upbeat story I can.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2814300421899202919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45846836" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45846836" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1045491-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45846836?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/1045491-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of historical fiction</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer45846836&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45846836" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11428194071918061925">Fantastic conclusion to Penman's Welsh trilogy. This book tells the story of Llewellyn the last and Simon de Montfort's children, who are inextricably linked due to the cruelties of England's King Edward Longshanks, son of the ineffectual King Henry, and Llewellyn's planned marriage to Eleanor (Ellen) de Motfort. The novel illuminates King Edward's medieval English version of manifest destiny and his ruthless desire to destroy Wales as an independent principality. <br/><br/>Penman does a masterful job at </span>
  <span id="freeText11428194071918061925" style="display:none">Fantastic conclusion to Penman's Welsh trilogy. This book tells the story of Llewellyn the last and Simon de Montfort's children, who are inextricably linked due to the cruelties of England's King Edward Longshanks, son of the ineffectual King Henry, and Llewellyn's planned marriage to Eleanor (Ellen) de Motfort. The novel illuminates King Edward's medieval English version of manifest destiny and his ruthless desire to destroy Wales as an independent principality. <br /><br />Penman does a masterful job at turning these historical figures, politics, and complex family relationships into an engaging story. The novel explores Llewellyn's tortured relationships with his brothers Owain, Davydd, and Rhodri, King Edward's relationship with his de Montfort kin, young Simon "Bran" de Montfort's guilt over his role in his father's death and the impact of the family's downfall on the de Montfort children. Penman's style made me root for Llewellyn and Ellen and become emotionally connected to them. By the end of the novel, even though the I knew that Wales ultimately becomes a part of England, I hoped that history would have gone another way and that King Edward would have let Wales survive on its own. The Reckoning is a masterful conclusion to a great trilogy. Unfortunately, history prevents it from having a happy ending; consequently the novel ends with shocking brutality. <br /><br />After I finished this novel I started Sunne in Splendour and I have the Eleanor of Aquitaine series on order. I've become a serious Sharon Kay Penman fan!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11428194071918061925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2351531006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2351531006?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/5239887-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2351531006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3645941820388870001">This book was dull by the pages several times. The author used commas where a connecting word would have made the reading better. At times I would have rated the book one star. At other times, all of the stars in the Milky Way would have been too few. Ms. Penman is an outstanding author. <br/><br/>I read the Welsh trilogy straight through without a break, and my favorite character was the last Prince Llewellyn. In his death scene, I wanted some super natural power to reattach his head to his body and let </span>
  <span id="freeText3645941820388870001" style="display:none">This book was dull by the pages several times. The author used commas where a connecting word would have made the reading better. At times I would have rated the book one star. At other times, all of the stars in the Milky Way would have been too few. Ms. Penman is an outstanding author. <br /><br />I read the Welsh trilogy straight through without a break, and my favorite character was the last Prince Llewellyn. In his death scene, I wanted some super natural power to reattach his head to his body and let him live for a few more pages. The Welsh aristocracy never caught a break, and their losses of kin, property and life made for such sad reading. That is life--people are born and then they die. What they are in the 'meantime' determines their legacy be it grand or be it of little consequence. The princes of Wales leave an enduring legacy that is unique. <br /><br /> In reading this trilogy, I focused on the aristocratic ladies who rubbed elbows with the princes. To my way of interpretation, the princes had an over abundance of charm. Thinking back, the princes' enemies were men. The women loved those men!<br /><br />Thank you, Ms. Penman, for a good read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3645941820388870001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_414145346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/414145346" />
    <a title="Helen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172797-helen"><img alt="Helen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358604934p2/5172797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/414145346?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen" href="/user/show/5172797-helen">Helen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer414145346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1342980856451500628">Two things spurred me to read this trilogy after I first became aware of it - the fact that although I had read a fair amount both fiction and non-fiction on the Tudors& Plantaganets, I had not ventured to the Welsh 'side of the story' so to speak - the other was because our Mum was Welsh. A blanket statement would be that I liked the books, which in a way was almost a given because of the subject matter; more succinctly put, I like her writing style. So, putting the two together and adding a so</span>
  <span id="freeText1342980856451500628" style="display:none">Two things spurred me to read this trilogy after I first became aware of it - the fact that although I had read a fair amount both fiction and non-fiction on the Tudors&amp; Plantaganets, I had not ventured to the Welsh 'side of the story' so to speak - the other was because our Mum was Welsh. A blanket statement would be that I liked the books, which in a way was almost a given because of the subject matter; more succinctly put, I like her writing style. So, putting the two together and adding a soupçon of historical accuracy embellished by her establishing a human aspect to the characters made these a really good read. Even though I knew of Simon de Montfort's horrific death at Evesham at the hands of Edward's men, it was brought home much more by reading of the reaction of his family and friends. Same with the death of LLewellyn ap Gryffudd, equally as horrific and almost more poignant because it also signalled the death of a dream &amp; a country. I suppose I am hooked.<br /><br />I have ordered Ms. Penman's Sunne in Splendour - given the discussion of Richard III I thought I might dust off my history &amp; for a (perhaps) different view of the Llewellyns, Edith Pargeter's The Brothers of Gwynned Quartet. <br /><br />It's the time of year to 'nest' with a good book &amp; a cuppa :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="1342980856451500628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/979746659?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susana" href="/user/show/8342113-susana">Susana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20693355-the-reckoning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8342113-susana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer979746659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10219422771587420612">This trilogy was a fantastic adventure! from king John and Llywelyn Fawr to king Edward longshanks and Llywelyn the last, it's been a heart wrenching experience. The magistral writing of SKP in this books achieves greatness. She takes the reader inside the story as an spectator, one can be witness of great moments in history and at the same time of the very personal lives of its characters. I came to love so many characters in this books, that almost dreaded to read the author's note were she wo</span>
  <span id="freeText10219422771587420612" style="display:none">This trilogy was a fantastic adventure! from king John and Llywelyn Fawr to king Edward longshanks and Llywelyn the last, it's been a heart wrenching experience. The magistral writing of SKP in this books achieves greatness. She takes the reader inside the story as an spectator, one can be witness of great moments in history and at the same time of the very personal lives of its characters. I came to love so many characters in this books, that almost dreaded to read the author's note were she would reveal which were total creation, and it blows me away how she endowed them to the point that they could've existed! <br />Trough Sharon learned about R3 and came to appreciate him as a great leader and a great man. Trough this trilogy I have found another great leader, one to admire and love, one I didn't know about: Simon the Montfort. Will learn more about him and his great reforms, spectacular character, masterfully depicted here by Sharon.<br />There's, in my opinion, no better way of learning history that trough SKP writing. Had an special time, loved every second of it and will definitely read more of Sharon's books. Fortunately she has many more for me to enjoy. So I have a happy and long tread before me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10219422771587420612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1377521034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16076549386572206620">In this novel, set in late 13th century, Sharon Kay Penman brings to life the final chapter in the English-Welsh wars, she proves as masterful and engaging storyteller as ever. <br/>I am rating this novel lower than previous novels of this trilogy (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77449.Here_be_Dragons__Welsh_Princes___1_' title='Here be Dragons (Welsh Princes, #1) by Sharon Kay Penman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here be Dragons</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_' title='Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falls the Shadow</a>) only because the story of Llewelyn ap Gruffydd and Helen de Montfort interesting as it is, cannot compete with the likes of Llewelyn Fawr and Joanna nor of Simon de Montfort and Nell. <br/>I’d highly recommend her books to oth</span>
  <span id="freeText16076549386572206620" style="display:none">In this novel, set in late 13th century, Sharon Kay Penman brings to life the final chapter in the English-Welsh wars, she proves as masterful and engaging storyteller as ever. <br />I am rating this novel lower than previous novels of this trilogy (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77449.Here_be_Dragons__Welsh_Princes___1_" title="Here be Dragons (Welsh Princes, #1) by Sharon Kay Penman" rel="nofollow noopener">Here be Dragons</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77448.Falls_the_Shadow__Welsh_Princes___2_" title="Falls the Shadow (Welsh Princes, #2) by Sharon Kay Penman" rel="nofollow noopener">Falls the Shadow</a>) only because the story of Llewelyn ap Gruffydd and Helen de Montfort interesting as it is, cannot compete with the likes of Llewelyn Fawr and Joanna nor of Simon de Montfort and Nell. <br />I’d highly recommend her books to other historical novels enthusiasts. 3.5 stars rounded up<br /><br />Fav. quotes:<br /><i><br />Drinking did not make men more amusing, it only made them think it did.<br /><br />What is forgiveness worth without trust?<br /><br />A man with a sense of divine mission is a very dangerous foe, indeed.<br /></i></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48964513" />
    <a title="Lori Anderson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/382208-lori-anderson"><img alt="Lori Anderson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555549941p2/382208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48964513?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori Anderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori Anderson" href="/user/show/382208-lori-anderson">Lori Anderson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">historical fiction fans, Diana Gabaldon fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382208-lori-anderson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382208-lori-anderson?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48964513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8248583414805879957">This book was heartbreakingly good. I've read three other books by Penman and each one is such a pleasure to read -- I look forward to my bedtime so much more (and go to bed even earlier!) because I have one of her thick books to read.<br/><br/>You probably already know how marvelous Penman is with her research, but she has a way of building the story that makes it seem so real -- well, real-er than a history book. I was so upset when certain characters died, so sure that they WOULDN'T die because it just</span>
  <span id="freeText8248583414805879957" style="display:none">This book was heartbreakingly good. I've read three other books by Penman and each one is such a pleasure to read -- I look forward to my bedtime so much more (and go to bed even earlier!) because I have one of her thick books to read.<br /><br />You probably already know how marvelous Penman is with her research, but she has a way of building the story that makes it seem so real -- well, real-er than a history book. I was so upset when certain characters died, so sure that they WOULDN'T die because it just wasn't TIME. I got emotionally involved in the book, which is one of my criteria for a Truly Great Book.<br /><br />Hope you'll read it!<br /><br />Lori Anderson<br /><br /><a href="http://www.lorianderson.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Lori Anderson:The Store</a> <br /><a href="http://www.lorianderson.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Things:The Blog</a> <br /><a href="http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=1152557235&amp;ref=profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></span>

<div id="review_2268044197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268044197" />
    <a title="Bob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6991670-bob"><img alt="Bob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545084294p2/6991670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268044197?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob" href="/user/show/6991670-bob">Bob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6991670-bob?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268044197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11669052970040171800"><i>Summary: Brings to a close the struggles between Wales and England under Edward I, the complicated relationship between brothers Llewellyn and David ab Gruffyd, and tells the story of the women who loved them--a true tale of love and loss.</i><br/><br/>Last month, I <a href='https://bobonbooks.com/2018/01/09/review-falls-the-shadow/' rel='nofollow noopener'>reviewed</a> the second volume of the Welsh Princes Trilogy, <i>Falls the Shadow</i>, which focused on Simon de Montfort and his campaign for the rights of the people with their king. In that book, the ongoing power struggle between the English and the Welsh</span>
  <span id="freeText11669052970040171800" style="display:none"><i>Summary: Brings to a close the struggles between Wales and England under Edward I, the complicated relationship between brothers Llewellyn and David ab Gruffyd, and tells the story of the women who loved them--a true tale of love and loss.</i><br /><br />Last month, I <a href="https://bobonbooks.com/2018/01/09/review-falls-the-shadow/" rel="nofollow noopener">reviewed</a> the second volume of the Welsh Princes Trilogy, <i>Falls the Shadow</i>, which focused on Simon de Montfort and his campaign for the rights of the people with their king. In that book, the ongoing power struggle between the English and the Welsh remains in the background. In The Reckoning, Penman brings the history of conflict between England and Wales to its culmination.<br /><br />Much of the story is told through the eyes of a young man, Hugh, who becomes squire to Bran de Montfort until his death of tertian fever in Italy, after which he serves Bran's sister Ellen, who had been betrothed to Llewellyn ab Gruffyd, Prince of Wales, until the death of her father Simon and the family's flight to France.<br /><br />Llewellyn has his own troubles. His mercurial brother Davydd has always coveted his power, even while Llewellyn, as did his grandfather, Llewellyn Fawr, understood that only a united Wales could have any hope of standing against English might. It is an odd relationship of brothers strangely drawn to each other, despite Davydd's betrayals, and alliance for a time with their hated enemy, Edward I, who, with the death of his feeble father, Henry III, is exerting his reign. Davydd marries Edward relation, Elizabeth at Edward's behest, a relation that blossoms into genuine love.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Llewellyn, fighting for Wales survival, and without an heir beside his betraying brother Davydd, revives his betrothal to Ellen, Simon and Nell's daughter. Ellen, her priest brother Amaury, and Hugh take a perilous sea voyage and are seized by "pirates" who are in fact in Edward's employ, and becomes a bargaining chip in the struggle, In the end, Llewellyn relents, is humbled and pays homage to Edward in return for the chance to marry Ellen.  He continues to hold Amaury to keep Llewellyn on his best behavior. Edward encroaches more and more on what were once Welsh domains and prerogatives, doing what Llewellyn had been unable to do--to unite Wales against the English and under his leadership.<br /><br />The story reaches a high point at Dolwyddelan in December of 1281. Despite an earlier plot to assassinate Llewellyn, foiled only by a freak storm, Davydd and Llewellyn have drawn close, and the other lords of Wales are ready to follow Llewellyn into rebellion. There is one other wonder, and it is that Ellen is with child--an heir for Llewellyn! Was this what goaded Davydd into initiating the rebellion before Llewellyn was ready?<br /><br />Edward I is a relentless foe, and the remainder of the story is one of heartbreak that I will leave to the reader. Only the love of the Squire Hugh, and Caitlin, the daughter of Davydd (a fictitious element) survives. Let us just say that it is from this period of time that the heir to the English crown is the Princ(ess) of Wales. <br /><br />Penman writes a gripping tale of two men, Edward and Llewellyn, who each love a country and idea. Only one could survive. Her characters and their relationships are complex, especially the relationship between Llewellyn and Davydd. So many of these people are related by blood or marriage and we see in Edward especially the tension of love and the ruthless use of power to achieve his ends. She paints a time where love could be passionate, especially in the knowledge that life was fragile and death could come in many guises, and often before one was ready. This is an older series, yet one that I hope remains in print. Penman, over these three volumes, tells the story of the ascent of the English kingship, and what was lost in the process.<br /><br />My <a href="https://bobonbooks.com/2015/07/17/review-here-be-dragons/" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> of <i>Here Be Dragons</i>.<br /><br />My <a href="https://bobonbooks.com/2018/01/09/review-falls-the-shadow/" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> of <i>Falls the Shadow</i>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11669052970040171800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16755778794284289438">This is a fantastic book - almost as good as Here Be Dragons. Great characters and a lot of hard-to-believe-they-really-happened events. While Llewelyn is easy to love (and rightfully so!), Davydd is the wonderful surprise character in this book. It's a great ending to the Welsh trilogy, and feels very full circle with Ellen and Llewelyn. But the ending . . . oof . . . so painful. </span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2549912330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5005272121435294937">Even though I read this end to the trilogy without reading the prior books, I was completely hooked in this story about the last Welsh Prince. That is what makes any of Penman's books so fantastic-the ability to take any event in history and make it so real. Every character, whether a main or secondary, was so wonderfully written that I cared about the fate of each and every one- leaving me crying for the last quarter of the story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3989408859934238172">In my memory, this third of the Welsh Trilogy was a bit of a re-tread and a bit weaker than the other two. On this reading, I found that I was much more engaged than in the second one, and much more gutted by the ending. A beautiful, well-written, education, meaty Historical Fiction. Nobody does this better than Sharon Kay Penman. </span>

    <a title="Brenda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5254166-brenda"><img alt="Brenda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308615060p2/5254166.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText6004658901893068776" style="display:none">"Penman's characters are so shrewdly imagined, so full of resonant human feeling that they seem to be on the page....Most compelling is the portrait of the Welsh as wild and rugged as their landscape."<br />SAN FRANCISCO CHRONICLE<br />Here, alive from the pages of history, is the compelling tale of a Celtic society ruled by Llewelyn, Prince of Wales, on a collison course with a feudal realm of Edward I. For everyone who has read the earlier books in this incomparable series or ever wanted to experience the rich tapestry of British history and lore, this bold and romantic adventure must be read.</span>
